      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP) compiles the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) of 189 countries in the annual <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a>. The index considers the health, education and income in the country to provide a measure of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(economics)" title="Human development (economics)">human development</a> which is comparable between countries and over time.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2020_trends_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_trends-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first human development index was published in 1990 with the goal to be a more comprehensive measure of human development than purely economic measures. The report chooses three key components of human development, longevity (later changed to "Long and healthy life"), knowledge and decent living standards. For each dimension an <a href="/wiki/Economic_indicator" title="Economic indicator">indicator</a> is chosen which in the 2020 report is <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">life expectancy at birth</a>; expected years of schooling for children and mean years of schooling for adults; and <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Income">Gross National Income</a> per capita respectively. The indicators are used to create a health index, an education index and an income index each with a value between 0 and 1. The <a href="/wiki/Geometric_mean" title="Geometric mean">geometric mean</a> of the three indexes, the cube root of the product of the indexes, is the human development index. A value above 0.800 is classified as very high, between 0.700 and 0.799 high, 0.550 to 0.699 as medium and anything below 0.550 as low.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-overview_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Technical_notes_2020_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Technical_notes_2020-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The data used to calculate HDI comes mostly from UN agencies and internation institutions such as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNDESA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDESA">UNDESA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> and <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>. Rarely when one of the indicators is missing cross-country regression models are used. Due to improved data and methodology updates HDI values are not comparable across human development reports.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Technical_notes_2020_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Technical_notes_2020-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Human Development index has several limitations in measuring the human development of countries including that it does not account for dimensions of human development such as inequality and participation in governance. It is also an average of large groups of people and can not show more granular development for different regions, ethnic groups or gender. <sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> To resolve one of the limitations the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a> (IHDI) was introduced in the 2010 report which stated that "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for inequality)" and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of 'potential' human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> To reflect developmental differences within countries a Subnational HDI (SHDI) was introduced in 2018 where the human development index is calculated in an internationally comparable way for over 1600 regions.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Countries_by_HDI">List of Countries by HDI</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:422px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_(2019),_score_changes.svg" class="image"><img alt="World map" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg/420px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg.png" decoding="async" width="420" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg/630px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg/840px-Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_%282019%29%2C_score_changes.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2911" data-file-height="1297"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_Human_Development_Index_(2019),_score_changes.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Change in score on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> from 2017 to 2018 (based on 2017 and 2018 data, published in 2019). 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994648498">
         <div class="div-col" style="-moz-column-width: 6em; -webkit-column-width: 6em; column-width: 6em; vertical-align:top; text-align:left;"> 
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
          <div class="legend">
           <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#00112B; color:white; -webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;+ 0.010
          </div>

         <th scope="col" data-sort-type="number">1990 data​<sup id="cite_ref-2020_region_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_region-12">[11]</a></sup> </th>
